class="NavContent hlist" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center">\n<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Goddard" title="Robert Goddard">Robert class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; background: transparent; text-align: left; padding-left: 5px; padding-top: 3px"><a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">Astronauts</a></div><div class="NavContent hlist" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Mercury_Seven" href="/wiki/NASA_Astronaut_Corps" title="NASA Astronaut Corps">NASA Astronaut Corps</a></li></ul></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:U.S._space_program_sidebar" title="Template:U.S. space program sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:U.S._space_program_sidebar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Template talk:U.S. space program sidebar (page does not exist)"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:U.S._space_program_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>National Aeronautics and Space Administration</b> (<b>NASA</b>, <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span><span title="/&#230;/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">&#230;</span><span title="\'s\' in \'sigh\'">s</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span></span>/</a></span></span>) is an <a href="/wiki/Independent_agencies_of_the_United_States_government" title="Independent agencies of the United States government">independent agency</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Federal_Government" title="United States Federal Government">United States Federal Government</a> responsible for the civilian <a href="/wiki/List_of_government_space_agencies" title="List of government space agencies">space program</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Aeronautics" title="Aeronautics">aeronautics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aerospace" title="Aerospace">aerospace</a> research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent_agency_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-independent_agency-7">[note 1]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/National_Aeronautics_and_Space_Act" title="National Aeronautics and Space Act">NASA was established</a> in 1958, succeeding the <a href="/wiki/National_Advisory_Committee_for_Aeronautics" title="National Advisory Committee for Aeronautics">National Advisory Committee for Aeronautics</a> (NACA). The new agency was to have a distinctly civilian orientation, encouraging peaceful applications in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_science" title="Space science">space science</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DDE_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-DDE-8">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-act1_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-act1-9">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NacaNASA_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-NacaNASA-10">[9]</a></sup> Since its establishment, most US <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">space exploration</a> efforts have been led by NASA, including the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">Apollo</a> <a href="/wiki/Moon_landing" title="Moon landing">Moon landing</a> missions, the <a href="/wiki/Skylab" title="Skylab">Skylab</a> space station, and later the <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">Space Shuttle</a>. NASA is supporting the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> and is overseeing the development of the <a href="/wiki/Orion_(spacecraft)" title="Orion (spacecraft)">Orion Multi-Purpose Crew Vehicle</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">Space Launch System</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Crew_Development" title="Commercial Crew Development">Commercial Crew</a> vehicles. The agency is also responsible for the <a href="/wiki/Launch_Services_Program" title="Launch Services Program">Launch Services Program</a> which provides oversight of launch operations and countdown management for unmanned NASA launches.\n</p><p>NASA science is focused on better understanding Earth through the <a href="/wiki/Earth_Observing_System" title="Earth Observing System">Earth Observing System</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> advancing <a href="/wiki/Heliophysics" title="Heliophysics">heliophysics</a> through the efforts of the <a href="/wiki/Science_Mission_Directorate" title="Science Mission Directorate">Science Mission Directorate</a>\'s Heliophysics Research Program;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup> exploring bodies throughout the <a href="/wiki/Solar_System" title="Solar System">Solar System</a> with advanced <a href="/wiki/Robotic_spacecraft" title="Robotic spacecraft">robotic spacecraft</a> missions such as <i><a href="/wiki/New_Horizons" title="New Horizons">New Horizons</a></i>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20150828_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20150828-13">[12]</a></sup> and researching <a href="/wiki/Astrophysics" title="Astrophysics">astrophysics</a> topics, such as the <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang" title="Big Bang">Big Bang</a>, through the <a href="/wiki/Great_Observatories_program" title="Great Observatories program">Great Observatories</a> and associated programs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" class="toctext">External links</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37"><a href="#General"><span class="tocnumber">15.1</span> <span class="toctext">General</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">15.2</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Creation">Creation</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Creation_of_NASA" title="Creation of NASA">Creation of NASA</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kennedy_Receives_Mariner_2_Model.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2206" data-file-width="2832" decoding="async" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Kennedy_Receives_Mariner_2_Model.jpg/310px-Kennedy_Receives_Mariner_2_Model.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Kennedy_Receives_Mariner_2_Model.jpg/465px-Kennedy_Receives_Mariner_2_Model.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Kennedy_Receives_Mariner_2_Model.jpg/620px-Kennedy_Receives_Mariner_2_Model.jpg 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kennedy_Receives_Mariner_2_Model.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bill_Pickering_(rocket_scientist)" title="Bill Pickering (rocket scientist)">William H. Pickering</a>, (center) JPL Director, President <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>, (right). NASA Administrator <a href="/wiki/James_E._Webb" title="James E. Webb">James E. Webb</a> (background) discussing the <a href="/wiki/Mariner_program" title="Mariner program">Mariner program</a>, with a model presented.</div></div></div>\n<p>From 1946, the <a href="/wiki/National_Advisory_Committee_for_Aeronautics" title="National Advisory Committee for Aeronautics">National Advisory Committee for Aeronautics</a> (NACA) had been experimenting with rocket planes such as the supersonic <a href="/wiki/Bell_X-1" title="Bell X-1">Bell X-1</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NACASupersonic_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-NACASupersonic-15">[14]</a></sup> In the early 1950s, there was challenge to launch an artificial satellite for the <a href="/wiki/International_Geophysical_Year" title="International Geophysical Year">International Geophysical Year</a> (1957&#8211;58). An effort for this was the American <a href="/wiki/Project_Vanguard" title="Project Vanguard">Project Vanguard</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_space_program" title="Soviet space program">Soviet</a> launch of the world\'s first artificial <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellite</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Sputnik_1" title="Sputnik 1">Sputnik 1</a></i>) on October 4, 1957, the attention of the United States turned toward its own fledgling space efforts. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">US Congress</a>, alarmed by the perceived threat to national security and technological leadership (known as the "<a href="/wiki/Sputnik_crisis" title="Sputnik crisis">Sputnik crisis</a>"), urged immediate and swift action; President <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a> and his advisers counseled more deliberate measures. On January 12, 1958, NACA organized a "Special Committee on Space Technology", headed by <a href="/wiki/Guyford_Stever" title="Guyford Stever">Guyford Stever</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NacaNASA_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-NacaNASA-10">[9]</a></sup> On January 14, 1958, NACA Director <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hugh_Dryden" title="Hugh Dryden">Hugh Dryden</a> published "A National Research Program for Space Technology" stating:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Erickson_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Erickson-16">[15]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><div class="PopUpMediaTransform" id="mwe_player_0" style="width:220px;" videopayload=\'&lt;div class="mediaContainer" style="width:854px"&gt;&lt;video id="mwe_player_1" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/NASA_60th-_How_It_All_Began.webm/854px--NASA_60th-_How_It_All_Began.webm.jpg" controls="" preload="none" autoplay="" style="width:854px;height:480px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="345.732" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="NASA_60th-_How_It_All_Began.webm" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/e/ef/NASA_60th-_How_It_All_Began.webm/NASA_60th-_How_It_All_Began.webm.480p.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;" data-title="SD WebM (480P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 480P" data-transcodekey="480p.webm" data-width="854" data-height="480" data-bandwidth="1107808" data-framerate="59.94"/&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/e/ef/NASA_60th-_How_It_All_Began.webm/NASA_60th-_How_It_All_Began.webm.480p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;" data-title="Small WebM (240P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 240P" data-transcodekey="240p.webm" data-width="426" data-height="240" data-bandwidth="330528" data-framerate="59.94"/&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/e/ef/NASA_60th-_How_It_All_Began.webm/NASA_60th-_How_It_All_Began.webm.240p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp9, opus&amp;quot;" data-title="Small VP9 (240P)" data-shorttitle="VP9 240P" data-transcodekey="240p.vp9.webm" data-width="426" data-height="240" data-bandwidth="385640" data-framerate="59.94"/&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/e/ef/NASA_60th-_How_It_All_Began.webm/NASA_60th-_How_It_All_Began.webm.360p.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;" data-title="WebM (360P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 360P" data-transcodekey="360p.webm" data-width="640" data-height="360" data-bandwidth="585456" data-framerate="59.94"/&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/e/ef/NASA_60th-_How_It_All_Began.webm/NASA_60th-_How_It_All_Began.webm.360p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp9, opus&amp;quot;" data-title="VP9 (360P)" data-shorttitle="VP9 360P" data-transcodekey="360p.vp9.webm" data-width="640" data-height="360" data-bandwidth="637512" data-framerate="59.94"/&gt;&lt;track src="https://commons.wikimedia.org/w/index.php?title=TimedText:NASA_60th-_How_It_All_Began.webm.en.srt&amp;amp;action=raw&amp;amp;ctype=text%2Fx-srt" kind="subtitles" type="text/x-srt" srclang="en" label="English (en) subtitles" data-mwtitle="TimedText:NASA_60th-_How_It_All_Began.webm.en.srt" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-dir="ltr"/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;\'><img alt="File:NASA 60th- How It All Began.webm" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/NASA_60th-_How_It_All_Began.webm/220px--NASA_60th-_How_It_All_Began.webm.jpg" style="width:220px;height:124px"/><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ef/NASA_60th-_How_It_All_Began.webm" target="new" title="Play media"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NASA_60th-_How_It_All_Began.webm" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A short documentary about the beginings of Nasa</div></div></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>It is of great urgency and importance to our country both from consideration of our prestige as a nation as well as military necessity that this challenge [<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sputnik" title="Sputnik">Sputnik</a></i>] be met by an energetic program of research and development for the conquest of space ... It is accordingly proposed that the scientific research be the responsibility of a national civilian agency ... NACA is capable, by rapid extension and expansion of its effort, of providing leadership in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_technology" title="Space technology">space technology</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Erickson_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-Erickson-16">[15]</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>While this new federal agency would conduct all non-military space activity, the <a href="/wiki/DARPA" title="DARPA">Advanced Research Projects Agency</a> (ARPA) was created in February 1958 to develop space technology for military application.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On July 29, 1958, Eisenhower signed the <a href="/wiki/National_Aeronautics_and_Space_Act" title="National Aeronautics and Space Act">National Aeronautics and Space Act</a>, establishing NASA. When it began operations on October 1, 1958, NASA absorbed the 43-year-old NACA intact; its 8,000 employees, an annual budget of US$100&#160;million, three major research laboratories (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Langley_Aeronautical_Laboratory" title="Langley Aeronautical Laboratory">Langley Aeronautical Laboratory</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ames_Aeronautical_Laboratory" title="Ames Aeronautical Laboratory">Ames Aeronautical Laboratory</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lewis_Flight_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Lewis Flight Propulsion Laboratory">Lewis Flight Propulsion Laboratory</a>) and two small test facilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Glennan_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Glennan-18">[17]</a></sup> A <a class="extiw" href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Logos_of_NASA" title="commons:Logos of NASA">NASA seal</a> was approved by President Eisenhower in 1959.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-order_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-order-19">[18]</a></sup> Elements of the <a href="/wiki/Army_Ballistic_Missile_Agency" title="Army Ballistic Missile Agency">Army Ballistic Missile Agency</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory" title="United States Naval Research Laboratory">United States Naval Research Laboratory</a> were incorporated into NASA. A significant contributor to NASA\'s entry into the <a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">Space Race</a> with the Soviet Union was the technology from the <a href="/wiki/V-2_rocket" title="V-2 rocket">German rocket program</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Wernher_von_Braun" title="Wernher von Braun">Wernher von Braun</a>, who was now working for the <a href="/wiki/Army_Ballistic_Missile_Agency" title="Army Ballistic Missile Agency">Army Ballistic Missile Agency</a> (ABMA), which in turn incorporated the technology of American scientist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Goddard" title="Robert Goddard">Robert Goddard</a>\'s earlier works.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-recoll_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-recoll-20">[19]</a></sup> Earlier research efforts within the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">US Air Force</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Glennan_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Glennan-18">[17]</a></sup> and many of ARPA\'s early space programs were also transferred to NASA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DARPA_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-DARPA-21">[20]</a></sup> In December 1958, NASA gained control of the <a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">Jet Propulsion Laboratory</a>, a contractor facility operated by the <a href="/wiki/California_Institute_of_Technology" title="California Institute of Technology">California Institute of Technology</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Glennan_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-Glennan-18">[17]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Staff_and_leadership">Staff and leadership</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Administrators_and_Deputy_Administrators_of_NASA" title="List of Administrators and Deputy Administrators of NASA">List of Administrators and Deputy Administrators of NASA</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jim_Bridenstine_official_portrait.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4406" data-file-width="3525" decoding="async" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Jim_Bridenstine_official_portrait.jpg/170px-Jim_Bridenstine_official_portrait.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Jim_Bridenstine_official_portrait.jpg/255px-Jim_Bridenstine_official_portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Jim_Bridenstine_official_portrait.jpg/340px-Jim_Bridenstine_official_portrait.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jim_Bridenstine_official_portrait.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jim Bridenstine official NASA portrait, April 26, 2018 at NASA Headquarters, Washington D.C.</div></div></div>\n<p>The agency\'s leader, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Administrators_and_Deputy_Administrators_of_NASA" title="List of Administrators and Deputy Administrators of NASA">NASA\'s administrator</a>, is nominated by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a> subject to approval of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">US Senate</a>, and reports to him or her and serves as senior space science advisor. Though space exploration is ostensibly non-partisan, the appointee usually is associated with the President\'s political party (<a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a>), and a new administrator is usually chosen when the Presidency changes parties. The only exceptions to this have been:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Democrat <a href="/wiki/Thomas_O._Paine" title="Thomas O. Paine">Thomas O. Paine</a>, acting administrator under Democrat <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a>, stayed on while Republican <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a> tried but failed to get one of his own choices to accept the job. Paine was confirmed by the Senate in March 1969 and served through September 1970.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Republican <a href="/wiki/James_C._Fletcher" title="James C. Fletcher">James C. Fletcher</a>, appointed by Nixon and confirmed in April 1971, stayed through May 1977 into the term of Democrat <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Daniel_Goldin" title="Daniel Goldin">Daniel Goldin</a> was appointed by Republican <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a> and stayed through the entire administration of Democrat <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>.</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_M._Lightfoot,_Jr." title="Robert M. Lightfoot, Jr.">Robert M. Lightfoot, Jr.</a>, associate administrator under Democrat <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, was kept on as acting administrator by Republican <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> until Trump\'s own choice <a href="/wiki/Jim_Bridenstine" title="Jim Bridenstine">Jim Bridenstine</a>, was confirmed in April 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_transition_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA_transition-23">[22]</a></sup> Though the agency is independent, the survival or discontinuation of projects can depend directly on the will of the President.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-24">[23]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>The first administrator was Dr. <a href="/wiki/T._Keith_Glennan" title="T. Keith Glennan">T. Keith Glennan</a> appointed by Republican President <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a>. During his term he brought together the disparate projects in American space development research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-glennan_biography_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-glennan_biography-25">[24]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The second administrator, <a href="/wiki/James_E._Webb" title="James E. Webb">James E. Webb</a> (1961&#8211;1968), appointed by President <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>, was a Democrat who first publicly served under President <a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman" title="Harry S. Truman">Harry S. Truman</a>. In order to implement the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">Apollo program</a> to achieve Kennedy\'s Moon landing goal by the end of the 1960s, Webb directed major management restructuring and facility expansion, establishing the Houston Manned Spacecraft (Johnson) Center and the Florida Launch Operations (Kennedy) Center. Capitalizing on Kennedy\'s legacy, President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lyndon_Johnson" title="Lyndon Johnson">Lyndon Johnson</a> kept continuity with the Apollo program by keeping Webb on when he succeeded Kennedy in November 1963. But Webb resigned in October 1968 before Apollo achieved its goal, and Republican President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richard_M._Nixon" title="Richard M. Nixon">Richard M. Nixon</a> replaced Webb with Republican <a href="/wiki/Thomas_O._Paine" title="Thomas O. Paine">Thomas O. Paine</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NASA_organigramm_November_2015.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/NASA_organigramm_November_2015.svg/220px-NASA_organigramm_November_2015.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/NASA_organigramm_November_2015.svg/330px-NASA_organigramm_November_2015.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/NASA_organigramm_November_2015.svg/440px-NASA_organigramm_November_2015.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NASA_organigramm_November_2015.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Organizational structure of NASA (2015)</div></div></div>\n<p>James Fletcher was responsible for early planning of the <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program" title="Space Shuttle program">Space Shuttle program</a> during his first term as administrator under President Nixon. He was appointed for a second term as administrator from May 1986 through April 1989 by President <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> to help the agency recover from the <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Challenger disaster">Space Shuttle <i>Challenger</i> disaster</a>.\n</p><p>Former <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">astronaut</a> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Bolden" title="Charles Bolden">Charles Bolden</a> served as NASA\'s twelfth administrator from July 2009 to January 20, 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-confirmed_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-confirmed-26">[25]</a></sup> Bolden is one of three former astronauts who became NASA administrators, along with <a href="/wiki/Richard_H._Truly" title="Richard H. Truly">Richard H. Truly</a> (served 1989&#8211;1992) and <a href="/wiki/Frederick_D._Gregory" title="Frederick D. Gregory">Frederick D. Gregory</a> (acting, 2005).\n</p><p>The agency\'s administration is located at <a href="/wiki/NASA_Headquarters" title="NASA Headquarters">NASA Headquarters</a> in Washington, DC and provides overall guidance and direction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HQ_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-HQ-27">[26]</a></sup> Except under exceptional circumstances, NASA civil service employees are required to be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Citizenship_in_the_United_States" title="Citizenship in the United States">citizens of the United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Space_flight_programs">Space flight programs</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_NASA_missions" title="List of NASA missions">List of NASA missions</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VonBraunMuellerReesSA6.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="562" data-file-width="720" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/VonBraunMuellerReesSA6.jpg/220px-VonBraunMuellerReesSA6.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/VonBraunMuellerReesSA6.jpg/330px-VonBraunMuellerReesSA6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/VonBraunMuellerReesSA6.jpg/440px-VonBraunMuellerReesSA6.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VonBraunMuellerReesSA6.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>At launch control for the May 28, 1964, <a href="/wiki/Saturn_I#Saturn_I_launches" title="Saturn I">Saturn I SA-6 launch</a>. <a href="/wiki/Wernher_von_Braun" title="Wernher von Braun">Wernher von Braun</a> is at center.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><div src="https://commons.wikimedia.org/w/index.php?title=TimedText:NASA_60th-_Humans_in_Space.webm.en.srt&amp;amp;action=raw&amp;amp;ctype=text%2Fx-srt" kind="subtitles" type="text/x-srt" srclang="en"
