codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;" data-title="WebM (360P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 360P" data-transcodekey="360p.webm" data-width="640" data-height="360" data-bandwidth="586856" data-framerate="59.94"/&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/4/49/NASA_60th-_What%E2%80%99s_Out_There.webm/NASA_60th-_What%E2%80%99s_Out_There.webm.360p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp9, opus&amp;quot;" data-title="VP9 (360P)" data-shorttitle="VP9 360P" data-transcodekey="360p.vp9.webm" data-width="640" data-height="360" data-bandwidth="588760" data-framerate="59.94"/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;\'><img alt="File:NASA 60th- What&#8217;s Out There.webm" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/NASA_60th-_What%E2%80%99s_Out_There.webm/220px--NASA_60th-_What%E2%80%99s_Out_There.webm.jpg" style="width:220px;height:124px"/><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/49/NASA_60th-_What%E2%80%99s_Out_There.webm" target="new" title="Play media"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NASA_60th-_What%E2%80%99s_Out_There.webm" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Many of the unmanned missions were used to explore the outer reaches of space as seen in this video</div></div></div>\n<p>Outside Mars, Jupiter was first visited by <i><a href="/wiki/Pioneer_10" title="Pioneer 10">Pioneer 10</a></i> in 1973. More than 20 years later <i><a href="/wiki/Galileo_(spacecraft)" title="Galileo (spacecraft)">Galileo</a></i> sent a probe into the planet\'s atmosphere, and became the first spacecraft to orbit the planet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PlanetSocJup_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-PlanetSocJup-119">[117]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Pioneer_11" title="Pioneer 11">Pioneer 11</a></i> became the first spacecraft to visit <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">Saturn</a> in 1979, with <i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">Voyager 2</a></i> making the first (and so far only) visits to <a href="/wiki/Uranus" title="Uranus">Uranus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neptune" title="Neptune">Neptune</a> in 1986 and 1989, respectively. The first spacecraft to leave the solar system was <i>Pioneer 10</i> in 1983. For a time it was the most distant spacecraft, but it has since been surpassed by both <i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_1" title="Voyager 1">Voyager 1</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">Voyager 2</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JPLVoyager_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-JPLVoyager-120">[118]</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>Pioneers 10</i> and <i>11</i> and both Voyager probes carry messages from the Earth to extraterrestrial life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASAPioneer10_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASAPioneer10-121">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JPLGolden_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-JPLGolden-122">[120]</a></sup> Communication can be difficult with deep space travel. For instance, it took about three hours for a radio signal to reach the <i>New Horizons</i> spacecraft when it was more than halfway to Pluto.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HeavensAbove_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-HeavensAbove-123">[121]</a></sup> Contact with <i>Pioneer 10</i> was lost in 2003. Both Voyager probes continue to operate as they explore the outer boundary between the Solar System and interstellar space.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASAVoyagesBeyond_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASAVoyagesBeyond-124">[122]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On November 26, 2011, NASA\'s <a href="/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory" title="Mars Science Laboratory">Mars Science Laboratory</a> mission was successfully launched for Mars. <i><a href="/wiki/Curiosity_(rover)" title="Curiosity (rover)">Curiosity</a></i> successfully landed on Mars on August 6, 2012, and subsequently began its search for evidence of past or present life on Mars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-MSL_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-MSL-125">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-MSL_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-MSL-126">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_York_Times_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-New_York_Times-127">[125]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Activities_.282010.E2.80.932017.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Activities_(2010&#8211;2017)">Activities (2010&#8211;2017)</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg/220px-Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg/330px-Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg/440px-Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Radioisotope within a graphite shell that goes into the generator.</div></div></div>\n<p>NASA\'s ongoing investigations include in-depth surveys of Mars (<a href="/wiki/Mars_2020" title="Mars 2020">Mars 2020</a> and <a href="/wiki/InSight" title="InSight">InSight</a>) and Saturn and studies of the Earth and the Sun. Other active spacecraft missions are <i><a href="/wiki/Juno_(spacecraft)" title="Juno (spacecraft)">Juno</a></i> for <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a>, <i>New Horizons</i> (for Jupiter, <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">Pluto</a>, and beyond), and <i><a href="/wiki/Dawn_(spacecraft)" title="Dawn (spacecraft)">Dawn</a></i> for the <a href="/wiki/Asteroid_belt" title="Asteroid belt">asteroid belt</a>. NASA continued to support <i><a href="/wiki/In_situ#Space-related" title="In situ">in situ</a></i> exploration beyond the asteroid belt, including Pioneer and Voyager traverses into the unexplored trans-Pluto region, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gas_Giant" title="Gas Giant">Gas Giant</a> orbiters <i>Galileo</i> (1989&#8211;2003), <i><a href="/wiki/Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens" title="Cassini&#8211;Huygens">Cassini</a></i>(1997&#8211;2017), and <i>Juno</i> (2011&#8211;). In the early 2000s, NASA was put on course for the Moon, however in 2010 this program was cancelled (see <a href="/wiki/Constellation_program" title="Constellation program">Constellation program</a>). As part of that plan the Shuttle was going to be replaced, however, although it was retired its replacement was also cancelled, leaving the US with no human spaceflight launcher for the first time in over three decades.\n</p><p>The <i><a href="/wiki/New_Horizons" title="New Horizons">New Horizons</a></i> mission to Pluto was launched in 2006 and successfully performed a flyby of <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">Pluto</a> on July 14, 2015. The probe received a <a href="/wiki/Gravity_assist" title="Gravity assist">gravity assist</a> from <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a> in February 2007, examining some of Jupiter\'s inner moons and testing on-board instruments during the flyby. On the horizon of NASA\'s plans is the <i><a href="/wiki/MAVEN" title="MAVEN">MAVEN</a></i> spacecraft as part of the <a href="/wiki/Mars_Scout_Program" title="Mars Scout Program">Mars Scout Program</a> to study the <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Mars" title="Atmosphere of Mars">atmosphere of Mars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MAVEN_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-MAVEN-128">[126]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On December 4, 2006, NASA announced it was planning a <a href="/wiki/Lunar_outpost_(NASA)" title="Lunar outpost (NASA)">permanent Moon base</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moon2_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-moon2-129">[127]</a></sup> The goal was to start building the Moon base by 2020, and by 2024, have a fully functional base that would allow for crew rotations and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/In-situ_resource_utilization" title="In-situ resource utilization">in-situ resource utilization</a>. However, in 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Review_of_United_States_Human_Space_Flight_Plans_Committee" title="Review of United States Human Space Flight Plans Committee">Augustine Committee</a> found the program to be on an "unsustainable trajectory."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup> In 2010, President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> halted existing plans, including the Moon base, and directed a generic focus on manned missions to asteroids and Mars, as well as extending support for the International Space Station.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[129]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since 2011, NASA\'s strategic goals have been<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NP-2011-01-699-HQ_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-NP-2011-01-699-HQ-132">[130]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Extend and sustain <a href="/wiki/Human_spaceflight" title="Human spaceflight">human activities</a> across the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_system" title="Solar system">solar system</a></li>\n<li>Expand scientific understanding of the Earth and the universe</li>\n<li>Create innovative new space <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Technologies" title="Technologies">technologies</a></li>\n<li>Advance <a href="/wiki/Aeronautics" title="Aeronautics">aeronautics</a> research</li>\n<li>Enable program and institutional capabilities to conduct NASA\'s aeronautics and space activities</li>\n<li>Share NASA with the public, educators, and students to provide opportunities to participate</li></ul>\n<p>In August 2011, NASA accepted the donation of <a href="/wiki/2012_National_Reconnaissance_Office_space_telescope_donation_to_NASA" title="2012 National Reconnaissance Office space telescope donation to NASA">two space telescopes</a> from the <a href="/wiki/National_Reconnaissance_Office" title="National Reconnaissance Office">National Reconnaissance Office</a>. Despite being stored unused, the instruments are superior to the <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">Hubble Space Telescope</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popsci-2012_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-popsci-2012-133">[131]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2011, NASA announced the start of the <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">Space Launch System</a> program to develop a human-rated heavy lift vehicle. The Space Launch System is intended to launch the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orion_Multi-Purpose_Crew_Vehicle" title="Orion Multi-Purpose Crew Vehicle">Orion Multi-Purpose Crew Vehicle</a> and other elements towards the <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Near-Earth_asteroids" title="Near-Earth asteroids">near-Earth asteroids</a>, and one day <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup> The Orion MPCV conducted an unmanned test launch on a <a href="/wiki/Delta_IV_Heavy" title="Delta IV Heavy">Delta IV Heavy</a> rocket in December 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/James_Webb_Space_Telescope" title="James Webb Space Telescope">James Webb Space Telescope</a> (JWST) is currently scheduled to launch in May 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg/220px-Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg/330px-Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg/440px-Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Curiosity_(rover)" title="Curiosity (rover)"><i>Curiosity</i></a>\'s wheel on <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a>, 2012</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pia21486curiowheelpopping.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="825" data-file-width="1446" decoding="async" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Pia21486curiowheelpopping.jpg/220px-Pia21486curiowheelpopping.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Pia21486curiowheelpopping.jpg/330px-Pia21486curiowheelpopping.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Pia21486curiowheelpopping.jpg/440px-Pia21486curiowheelpopping.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pia21486curiowheelpopping.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Curiosity</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'</span>s battered wheel after several years of exploration, 2017</div></div></div>\n<p>On August 6, 2012, NASA landed the rover <i><a href="/wiki/Curiosity_(rover)" title="Curiosity (rover)">Curiosity</a></i> on Mars. On August 27, 2012, <i>Curiosity</i> transmitted the first pre-recorded message from the surface of Mars back to Earth, made by Administrator Charlie Bolden:\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Hello. This is Charlie Bolden, NASA Administrator, speaking to you via the broadcast capabilities of the <i>Curiosity</i> rover, which is now on the surface of Mars.\n</p><p>Since the beginning of time, humankind\'s curiosity has led us to constantly seek new life ... new possibilities just beyond the horizon. I want to congratulate the men and women of our NASA family as well as our commercial and government partners around the world, for taking us a step beyond to Mars.\n</p><p>This is an extraordinary achievement. Landing a rover on Mars is not easy&#160;&#8211; others have tried&#160;&#8211; only America has fully succeeded. The investment we are making ... the knowledge we hope to gain from our observation and analysis of Gale Crater, will tell us much about the possibility of life on Mars as well as the past and future possibilities for our own planet. <i>Curiosity</i> will bring benefits to Earth and inspire a new generation of scientists and explorers, as it prepares the way for a human mission in the not too distant future. Thank you.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup>\n</p>\n</blockquote>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_and_planned_activities">Recent and planned activities</span></h3>\n<p>NASA\'s ongoing investigations include in-depth surveys of Mars (<a href="/wiki/Mars_2020" title="Mars 2020">Mars 2020</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/InSight" title="InSight">InSight</a></i>) and Saturn and studies of the Earth and the Sun. Other active spacecraft missions are <i><a href="/wiki/Juno_(spacecraft)" title="Juno (spacecraft)">Juno</a></i> for <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a>, <i>New Horizons</i> (for Jupiter, <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">Pluto</a>, and beyond), and <i><a href="/wiki/Dawn_(spacecraft)" title="Dawn (spacecraft)">Dawn</a></i> for the <a href="/wiki/Asteroid_belt" title="Asteroid belt">asteroid belt</a>. NASA continued to support <i><a href="/wiki/In_situ#Space-related" title="In situ">in situ</a></i> exploration beyond the asteroid belt, including Pioneer and Voyager traverses into the unexplored trans-Pluto region, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gas_Giant" title="Gas Giant">Gas Giant</a> orbiters <i>Galileo</i> (1989&#8211;2003), <i><a href="/wiki/Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens" title="Cassini&#8211;Huygens">Cassini</a></i> (1997&#8211;2017), and <i>Juno</i> (2011&#8211;).\n</p><p>The <i><a href="/wiki/New_Horizons" title="New Horizons">New Horizons</a></i> mission to Pluto was launched in 2006 and successfully performed a flyby of <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">Pluto</a> on July 14, 2015. The probe received a <a href="/wiki/Gravity_assist" title="Gravity assist">gravity assist</a> from <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a> in February 2007, examining some of Jupiter\'s inner moons and testing on-board instruments during the flyby. On the horizon of NASA\'s plans is the <i><a href="/wiki/MAVEN" title="MAVEN">MAVEN</a></i> spacecraft as part of the <a href="/wiki/Mars_Scout_Program" title="Mars Scout Program">Mars Scout Program</a> to study the <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Mars" title="Atmosphere of Mars">atmosphere of Mars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MAVEN_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-MAVEN-128">[126]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2017, President <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Donald_Trump" title="Presidency of Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> directed NASA to send Humans to Mars by the year 2033.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-futurism.com_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-futurism.com-111">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-businessinsider.com_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-businessinsider.com-138">[136]</a></sup>  Foci in general for NASA were noted as human space exploration, space science, and technology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-businessinsider.com_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-businessinsider.com-138">[136]</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Europa_Clipper" title="Europa Clipper">Europa Clipper</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Mars_2020" title="Mars 2020">Mars 2020</a> continue to be supported for their planned schedules.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2018, NASA alongside with other companies including <a href="/wiki/Sensor_Coating_Systems" title="Sensor Coating Systems">Sensor Coating Systems</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pratt_%26_Whitney" title="Pratt &amp; Whitney">Pratt &amp; Whitney</a>, Monitor Coating and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Technologies_Corp" title="United Technologies Corp">UTRC</a> have launched the project CAUTION (CoAtings for Ultra High Temperature detectION). This project aims to enhance the temperature range of the <a href="/wiki/Thermal_history_coating" title="Thermal history coating">Thermal History Coating</a> up to 1,500C and beyond. The final goal of this project is improving the safety of jet engines as well as increasing efficiency and reducing CO2 emissions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Recent and planned activities include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/InSight" title="InSight">InSight</a></i>, launched and landed on Mars in 2018</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/New_Horizons" title="New Horizons">New Horizons</a></i>, Kuiper belt object <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/(486958)_2014_MU69" title="(486958) 2014 MU69">(486958) 2014 MU<span style="position: relative; top: 0.3em;"><span style="font-size:80%;">69</span></span></a></span> flyby on January 1, 2019<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20181231-kc_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20181231-kc-141">[139]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/OSIRIS-REx" title="OSIRIS-REx">Osiris-Rex</a>, en route for asteroid sample return on September 24, 2023<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Mars 2020 rover (planned)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup></li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Europa_Clipper" title="Europa Clipper">Europa Clipper</a></i> (planned)</li>\n<li>Misc. Discovery Missions<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>\n<li>Misc. Explorer Missions<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>\n<li>New Frontier mission including New Horizons, Juno, and Osiris-Rex<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>\n<li>Earth Observation, Solar and Astronomical observatories<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/James_Webb_Space_Telescope" title="James Webb Space Telescope">James Webb Space Telescope</a> (planned)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Parker_Solar_Probe" title="Parker Solar Probe">Parker Solar Probe</a>, launched August 2018</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Transiting_Exoplanet_Survey_Satellite" title="Transiting Exoplanet Survey Satellite">Transiting Exoplanet Survey Satellite</a> (TESS), launched in April 2018</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Wide_Field_Infrared_Survey_Telescope" title="Wide Field Infrared Survey Telescope">Wide Field Infrared Survey Telescope</a> (WFIRST) (planned)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="NASA_Advisory_Council">NASA Advisory Council</span></h2>\n<p>In response to the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_1" title="Apollo 1">Apollo 1</a> accident which killed three astronauts in 1967, Congress directed NASA to form an Aerospace Safety Advisory Panel (ASAP) to advise the NASA Administrator on safety issues and hazards in NASA\'s aerospace programs. In the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">Shuttle <i>Columbia</i> disaster</a>, Congress required that the ASAP submit an annual report to the NASA Administrator and to Congress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup> By 1971, NASA had also established the Space Program Advisory Council and the Research and Technology Advisory Council to provide the administrator with advisory committee support. In 1977, the latter two were combined to form the NASA Advisory Council (NAC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAC_About_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-NAC_About-146">[144]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Aeronautics_and_Space_Administration_Authorization_Act_of_2014" title="National Aeronautics and Space Administration Authorization Act of 2014">National Aeronautics and Space Administration Authorization Act of 2014</a> reaffirmed the importance of ASAP.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Directives">Directives</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Space_policy_of_the_United_States" title="Space policy of the United States">Space policy of the United States</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Artist%27s_Conception_of_Space_Station_Freedom_-_GPN-2003-00092.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2292" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Artist%27s_Conception_of_Space_Station_Freedom_-_GPN-2003-00092.jpg/220px-Artist%27s_Conception_of_Space_Station_Freedom_-_GPN-2003-00092.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Artist%27s_Conception_of_Space_Station_Freedom_-_GPN-2003-00092.jpg/330px-Artist%27s_Conception_of_Space_Station_Freedom_-_GPN-2003-00092.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Artist%27s_Conception_of_Space_Station_Freedom_-_GPN-2003-00092.jpg/440px-Artist%27s_Conception_of_Space_Station_Freedom_-_GPN-2003-00092.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Artist%27s_Conception_of_Space_Station_Freedom_-_GPN-2003-00092.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Artistic rendition of Space Station Freedom with the Orbiter Vehicle</div></div></div>\n<p>Some of the major NASA directives were to land people on the Moon, build the Space Shuttle, and build a large space station. Typically, the major directives had the intervention of the science advisory, political, funding, and public interest that synergized into various waves of effort often heavily swayed by technical, funding, and worldwide events. For example, there was a major push to build <a href="/wiki/Space_Station_Freedom" title="Space Station Freedom">Space Station Freedom</a> in the 1980s, but when the Cold War ended, the Russians, the Americans and other international partners came together to build the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a>.\n</p><p>In the 2010s, the major shift was the retirement of the <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">Space Shuttle</a> and the development of a new manned heavy lift rocket, the <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">Space Launch System</a>. Missions for the new System have varied but overall, they were similar as it primarily involved the desire to send a human into the space. The <a href="/wiki/Space_Exploration_Initiative" title="Space Exploration Initiative">Space Exploration Initiative</a> of the 1980s opened newer avenues of galaxy exploration.\n</p><p>In the coming decades, the focus is gradually shifting towards exploration of planet Mars; however, some differences exist over the technologies to develop and focus on for the exploration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-space.com_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-space.com-147">[145]</a></sup> One of the options considered was the <a href="/wiki/Asteroid_Redirect_Mission" title="Asteroid Redirect Mission">Asteroid Redirect Mission</a> (ARM).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-space.com_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-space.com-147">[145]</a></sup> ARM had largely been defunded in 2017, but the key technologies developed for ARM would be utilized for future exploration, especially on a solar electric propulsion system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-defunded_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-defunded-148">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-space.com_147-2"><a href="#cite_note-space.com-147">[145]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Longer project execution timelines means it is up to future officials to execute on a directive, which often leads to directional mismanagement. For example, a Shuttle replacement has numerous components involved, each making some headway before being called off for various reasons including the National Aerospace Plane, Venture Star, Orbital Space Plane, Ares I, and others. The asteroid mission was not a major directive in the 2010s. Instead, the general support rested with the long-term goal of getting humans to Mars. The space shuttle was retired and much of the existing road map was shelved including the then planned Lunar Return and Ares I human launch vehicle.\n</p><p>Previously, in the early 2000s, there was a plan called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constellation_Program" title="Constellation Program">Constellation Program</a> but this was defunded in the early 2010s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_cancels_Moon_return_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_cancels_Moon_return-149">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FY2011_budget_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-FY2011_budget-150">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WashPost_eliminates_funds_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-WashPost_eliminates_funds-151">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[150]</a></sup> In the 1990s, there was a plan called "Faster, Better, Cheaper"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup> In the 1980s, there was a directive to build a manned space station.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[152]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="NASA_Authorization_Act_of_2017">NASA Authorization Act of 2017</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Orion_ISS_1_(05-2007).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1920" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Orion_ISS_1_%2805-2007%29.jpg/220px-Orion_ISS_1_%2805-2007%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Orion_ISS_1_%2805-2007%29.jpg/330px-Orion_ISS_1_%2805-2007%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Orion_ISS_1_%2805-2007%29.jpg/440px-Orion_ISS_1_%2805-2007%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Orion_ISS_1_(05-2007).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Orion at ISS artwork</div></div></div>\n<p>The NASA Authorization Act of 2017, which included $19.5 billion in funding for that fiscal year, directed NASA to get humans near or on the surface of Mars by the early 2030s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Space_Policy_Directive_1">Space Policy Directive 1</span></h3>\n<p>In December 2017, on the 45th anniversary of the last manned mission to the Lunar surface, President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> approved a directive that includes a lunar mission on the pathway to Mars and beyond.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-space.com_147-3"><a href="#cite_note-space.com-147">[145]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>We\'ll learn.  The directive I\'m signing today will refocus America\'s space program on human exploration and discovery.  It marks an important step in returning American astronauts to the Moon for the first time since 1972 for long-term exploration and use.  This time, we will not only plant our flag and leave our footprint, we will establish a foundation for an eventual mission to Mars.  And perhaps, someday, to many worlds beyond.</p><div class="templatequotecite">&#8212;&#8201;<cite>President Donald Trump, 2017<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spo20171217_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-spo20171217-156">[154]</a></sup></cite></div>\n</blockquote>\n<p>New NASA administrator <a href="/wiki/Jim_Bridenstine" title="Jim Bridenstine">Jim Bridenstine</a> addressed this directive in an August 2018 speech where he focused on the sustainability aspects&#8212;going to the Moon to stay&#8212;that are explicit in the directive, including taking advantage of US commercial space <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reusable_launch_vehicle" title="Reusable launch vehicle">capability</a> that did not exist even five years ago, which have <a href="/wiki/Space_launch_market_competition" title="Space launch market competition">driven down costs</a> and increased access to space.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa20180829_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-nasa20180829-157">[155]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/NASA_research" title="NASA research">NASA research</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For technologies funded or otherwise supported by NASA, see <a href="/wiki/NASA_spinoff_technologies" title="NASA spinoff technologies">NASA spinoff technologies</a>.</div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AX-5-spacesuit.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1752" data-file-width="1037" decoding="async" height="372" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/AX-5-spacesuit.jpg/220px-AX-5-spacesuit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/AX-5-spacesuit.jpg/330px-AX-5-spacesuit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/AX-5-spacesuit.jpg/440px-AX-5-spacesuit.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AX-5-spacesuit.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>NASA developed this hard-suit in the 1980s at the Ames Research Center</div></div></div>\n<p>NASA\'s <a href="/wiki/Aeronautics_Research_Mission_Directorate" title="Aeronautics Research Mission Directorate">Aeronautics Research Mission Directorate</a> conducts aeronautics research.\n</p><p>NASA has made use of technologies such as the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multi-Mission_Radioisotope_Thermoelectric_Generator" title="Multi-Mission Radioisotope Thermoelectric Generator">Multi-Mission Radioisotope Thermoelectric Generator</a></i> (MMRTG), which is a type of <a href="/wiki/Radioisotope_thermoelectric_generator" title="Radioisotope thermoelectric generator">Radioisotope thermoelectric generator</a> used on space missions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup> Shortages of this material have curtailed deep space missions since the turn of the millennia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lpi.usra.edu_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-lpi.usra.edu-159">[157]</a></sup> An example of a spacecraft that was not developed because of a shortage of this material was <i><a href="/wiki/New_Horizons_2" title="New Horizons 2">New Horizons 2</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lpi.usra.edu_159-1"><a href="#cite_note-lpi.usra.edu-159">[157]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Earth science research program was created and first funded in the 1980s under the administrations of <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_H.W._Bush" title="George H.W. Bush">George H.W. Bush</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[159]</a></sup>\n</p><p>NASA started an annual competition in 2014 named <i>Cubes in Space</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[160]</a></sup> It is jointly organized by NASA and the global education company <i>I Doodle Learning</i>, with the objective of teaching school students aged 11&#8211;18 to design and build scientific experiments to be launched into space on a NASA rocket or balloon. On June 21, 2017 the world\'s smallest satellite, <a href="/wiki/Kalam_SAT" title="Kalam SAT">Kalam SAT</a>, built by an Indian team, was launched.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_study">Climate study</span></h3>\n<p>NASA also researches and publishes on <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[161]</a></sup> Its statements concur with the global scientific consensus that the global climate is warming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[162]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Smith_Walker" title="Robert Smith Walker">Bob Walker</a>, who has advised the 45th President of the United States <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> on space issues, has advocated that NASA should focus on space exploration and that its climate study operations should be transferred to other agencies such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NOAA" title="NOAA">NOAA</a>. Former NASA atmospheric scientist <a href="/wiki/J._Marshall_Shepherd" title="J. Marshall Shepherd">J. Marshall Shepherd</a> countered that Earth science study was built into NASA\'s mission at <a href="/wiki/Creation_of_NASA" title="Creation of NASA">its creation</a> in the 1958 <a href="/wiki/National_Aeronautics_and_Space_Act" title="National Aeronautics and Space Act">National Aeronautics and Space Act</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[163]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">Facilities</span></h2>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:348px;max-width:348px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:172px;max-width:172px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg"><img alt="Jet Propulsion Laboratory complex in Pasadena, California" data-file-height="2242" data-file-width="2867" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg/170px-Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg/255px-Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg/340px-Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">Jet Propulsion Laboratory</a> complex in Pasadena, California</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:172px;max-width:172px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg"><img alt="Vehicle Assembly Building and Launch Control Center at Kennedy Space Center" data-file-height="1151" data-file-width="1499" decoding="async" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg/170px-Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg/255px-Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg/340px-Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Vehicle Assembly and Launch Control at <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">Kennedy Space Center</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/NASA_facilities" title="NASA facilities">NASA facilities</a></div>\n<p>NASA\'s facilities are research, construction and communication centers to help its missions. Some facilities serve more than one application for historic or administrative reasons. NASA also operates a <a href="/wiki/NASA_Railroad" title="NASA Railroad">short-line railroad</a> at the Kennedy Space Center and uses special aircraft.\n</p><p>John F. Kennedy Space Center (KSC), is one of the best-known NASA facilities. It has been the launch site for every United States human space flight since 1968. Although such flights are currently on pause, KSC continues to manage and operate unmanned rocket launch facilities for America\'s civilian space program from three pads at the adjoining Cape Canaveral Air Force Station.\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson_Space_Center" title="Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center">Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center</a> (JSC) in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a> is home to the <a href="/wiki/Christopher_C._Kraft_Jr._Mission_Control_Center" title="Christopher C. Kraft Jr. Mission Control Center">Christopher C. Kraft Jr. Mission Control Center</a>, where all flight control is managed for manned space missions. JSC is the lead NASA center for activities regarding the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> and also houses the <a href="/wiki/NASA_Astronaut_Corps" title="NASA Astronaut Corps">NASA Astronaut Corps</a> that selects, trains, and provides astronauts as crew members for US and international space missions.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2832" data-file-width="4256" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg/220px-STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg/330px-STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg/440px-STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Christopher_C._Kraft_Jr._Mission_Control_Center#FCR_1_(2006-present)" title="Christopher C. Kraft Jr. Mission Control Center">FCR 1</a> in 2009 during the <a href="/wiki/STS-128" title="STS-128">STS-128</a> mission, JSC in Houston</div></div></div>\n<p>Another major facility is <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Space_Flight_Center" title="Marshall Space Flight Center">Marshall Space Flight Center</a> in Huntsville, Alabama at which the Saturn 5 rocket and Skylab were developed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASAMSFC_Fact_sheet_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASAMSFC_Fact_sheet-166">[164]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">JPL</a> worked together with <a href="/wiki/Army_Ballistic_Missile_Agency" title="Army Ballistic Missile Agency">ABMA</a>, one of the agencies behind <a href="/wiki/Explorer_1" title="Explorer 1">Explorer 1</a>, the first American space mission.\n</p><p>The ten NASA field centers are:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Space_Center" title="John F. Kennedy Space Center">John F. Kennedy Space Center</a>, Florida</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ames_Research_Center" title="Ames Research Center">Ames Research Center</a>, Moffett Field, California</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Armstrong_Flight_Research_Center" title="Armstrong Flight Research Center">Armstrong Flight Research Center</a> (formerly Hugh L. Dryden Flight Research Facility), Edwards, California</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Goddard_Space_Flight_Center" title="Goddard Space Flight Center">Goddard Space Flight Center</a>, Greenbelt, Maryland</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">Jet Propulsion Laboratory</a>, near Pasadena, California</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson_Space_Center" title="Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center">Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center</a>, Houston, Texas</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Langley_Research_Center" title="Langley Research Center">Langley Research Center</a>, Hampton, Virginia</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_H._Glenn_Research_Center" title="John H. Glenn Research Center">John H. Glenn Research Center</a>, Cleveland, Ohio</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_C._Marshall_Space_Flight_Center" title="George C. Marshall Space Flight Center">George C. Marshall Space Flight Center</a>, Huntsville, Alabama</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/John_C._Stennis_Space_Center" title="John C. Stennis Space Center">John C. Stennis Space Center</a>, Bay St. Louis, Mississippi</li></ul>\n<p>Numerous other facilities are operated by NASA, including the <a href="/wiki/Wallops_Flight_Facility" title="Wallops Flight Facility">Wallops Flight Facility</a> in Wallops Island, Virginia; the <a href="/wiki/Michoud_Assembly_Facility" title="Michoud Assembly Facility">Michoud Assembly Facility</a> in New Orleans, Louisiana; the <a href="/wiki/White_Sands_Test_Facility" title="White Sands Test Facility">White Sands Test Facility</a> in Las Cruces, New Mexico; and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deep_Space_Network" title="Deep Space Network">Deep Space Network</a> stations in <a href="/wiki/Goldstone_Deep_Space_Communications_Complex" title="Goldstone Deep Space Communications Complex">Barstow</a>, California; <a href="/wiki/Madrid_Deep_Space_Communications_Complex" title="Madrid Deep Space Communications Complex">Madrid</a>, Spain; and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canberra_Deep_Space_Communications_Complex" title="Canberra Deep Space Communications Complex">Canberra</a>, Australia.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Budget">Budget</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NASA-Budget-Federal.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="589" data-file-width="1151" decoding="async" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/NASA-Budget-Federal.svg/220px-NASA-Budget-Federal.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/NASA-Budget-Federal.svg/330px-NASA-Budget-Federal.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/NASA-Budget-Federal.svg/440px-NASA-Budget-Federal.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NASA-Budget-Federal.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>NASA\'s budget from 1958 to 2012 as a percentage of federal budget</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jsc2004e18852.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3555" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Jsc2004e18852.jpg/220px-Jsc2004e18852.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Jsc2004e18852.jpg/330px-Jsc2004e18852.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Jsc2004e18852.jpg/440px-Jsc2004e18852.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jsc2004e18852.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An artist\'s conception, from NASA, of an astronaut planting a US flag on Mars. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manned_mission_to_Mars" title="Manned mission to Mars">manned mission to Mars</a> has been discussed as a possible NASA mission since the 1960s.</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Budget_of_NASA" title="Budget of NASA">Budget of NASA</a></div>\n<p>NASA\'s share of the total federal budget peaked at approximately 4.41% in 1966 during the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">Apollo program</a>, then rapidly declined to approximately 1% in 1975, and stayed around that level through 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-24">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup> The percentage then gradually dropped, until leveling off again at around half a percent in 2006 (estimated in 2012 at 0.48% of the federal budget).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B2013_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-B2013-168">[166]</a></sup> In a March 2012 hearing of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_Commerce,_Science_and_Transportation" title="United States Senate Committee on Commerce, Science and Transportation">United States Senate Science Committee</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Science_communicator" title="Science communicator">science communicator</a> <a href="/wiki/Neil_deGrasse_Tyson" title="Neil deGrasse Tyson">Neil deGrasse Tyson</a> testified that "Right now, NASA\'s annual budget is half a penny on your tax dollar. For twice that&#8212;a penny on a dollar&#8212;we can transform the country from a sullen, dispirited nation, weary of economic struggle, to one where it has reclaimed its 20th century birthright to dream of tomorrow."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tysontranscript_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-tysontranscript-169">[167]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tysontranscript_video_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-tysontranscript_video-170">[168]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Despite this, public perception of NASA\'s budget differs significantly: a 1997 poll indicated that most Americans believed that 20% of the federal budget went to NASA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perception_of_US_Human_Spaceflight_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-perception_of_US_Human_Spaceflight-171">[169]</a></sup>\n</p><p>For Fiscal Year 2015, NASA received an appropriation of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$18.01 billion</span> from Congress&#8212;$549 million more than requested and approximately $350 million more than the 2014 NASA budget passed by Congress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfn20141214_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-sfn20141214-172">[170]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In Fiscal Year 2016, NASA received $19.3 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-businessinsider.com_138-2"><a href="#cite_note-businessinsider.com-138">[136]</a></sup>\n</p><p>President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> signed the NASA Transition Authorization Act of 2017 in March, which set the 2017 budget at around $19.5 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-businessinsider.com_138-3"><a href="#cite_note-businessinsider.com-138">[136]</a></sup> The budget is also reported as $19.3 billion for 2017, with $20.7 billion proposed for FY2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FY2018_proposal_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-FY2018_proposal-173">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20.7_billion_SN_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-20.7_billion_SN-174">[172]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Examples of some proposed FY2018 budgets:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20.7_billion_SN_174-1"><a href="#cite_note-20.7_billion_SN-174">[172]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Exploration: $4.79 billion</li>\n<li>Planetary science: $2.23 billion</li>\n<li>Earth science: $1.92 billion</li>\n<li>Aeronautics: $0.685 billion</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_impact">Environmental impact</span></h2>\n<p>The exhaust gases produced by rocket propulsion systems, both in Earth\'s atmosphere and in space, can adversely effect the Earth\'s environment. Some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hypergolic" title="Hypergolic">hypergolic</a> rocket propellants, such as <a href="/wiki/Hydrazine" title="Hydrazine">hydrazine</a>, are highly toxic prior to <a href="/wiki/Combustion" title="Combustion">combustion</a>, but decompose into less toxic compounds after burning. Rockets using hydrocarbon fuels, such as <a href="/wiki/Kerosene" title="Kerosene">kerosene</a>, release carbon dioxide and soot in their exhaust.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rocket_soot_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-rocket_soot-175">[173]</a></sup> However, carbon dioxide emissions are insignificant compared to those from other sources; on average, the United States consumed 802,620,000 US gallons (3.0382<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup>9</sup>&#160;L) gallons of liquid fuels per day in 2014, while a single <a href="/wiki/Falcon_9" title="Falcon 9">Falcon 9</a> rocket first stage burns around 25,000 US gallons (95,000&#160;L) of <a href="/wiki/Kerosene" title="Kerosene">kerosene</a> fuel per launch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIA_2016_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-EIA_2016-176">[174]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[175]</a></sup> Even if a Falcon 9 were launched every single day, it would only represent 0.006% of liquid fuel consumption (and carbon dioxide emissions) for that day. Additionally, the exhaust from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LOx" title="LOx">LOx</a>- and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LH2" title="LH2">LH2</a>- fueled engines, like the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SSME" title="SSME">SSME</a>, is almost entirely water vapor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-SSME_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-SSME-178">[176]</a></sup> NASA addressed environmental concerns with its canceled <a href="/wiki/Constellation_program" title="Constellation program">Constellation program</a> in accordance with the National Environmental Policy Act in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-Constellation_Program_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-Constellation_Program-179">[177]</a></sup> In contrast, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ion_engines" title="Ion engines">ion engines</a> use harmless noble gases like <a href="/wiki/Xenon" title="Xenon">xenon</a> for propulsion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ns20070928_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-ns20070928-180">[178]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goto2003_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-Goto2003-181">[179]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On May 8, 2003, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">Environmental Protection Agency</a> recognized NASA as the first federal agency to directly use <a href="/wiki/Landfill_gas" title="Landfill gas">landfill gas</a> to produce energy at one of its facilities&#8212;the <a href="/wiki/Goddard_Space_Flight_Center" title="Goddard Space Flight Center">Goddard Space Flight Center</a>, Greenbelt, Maryland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup>\n</p><p>An example of NASA\'s environmental efforts is the <a href="/wiki/NASA_Sustainability_Base" title="NASA Sustainability Base">NASA Sustainability Base</a>. Additionally, the Exploration Sciences Building was awarded the LEED Gold rating in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[181]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gallery">Gallery</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Observations">Observations</span></h3>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional center">\n<li planetary-sized objects. Other major targets of study are the Earth itself, the Sun, and smaller Solar System bodies like asteroids and comets. href="#cite_ref-independent_agency_7-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">NASA is an independent agency that is not a part of any <a href="/wiki/United_States_federal_executive_departments" title="United States federal executive departments">executive department</a> but reports directly to the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-47"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-47">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The descend stage of the LM stayed on the Moon after landing while the ascend stage brought the two astronauts back to the CSM and then fell back to the Moon.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-184"><span
